<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bb4cf02d-01ad-4184-940e-8d5f0056054c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer9707419036562585626">In the middle of the night, a controversial U.S. senator is found murdered in bed in his Georgetown pied-a-terre. The police turn up only one clue: a mysterious rhyme signed "Jack and Jill" promising that this is just the beginning. Jack and Jill are out to get the rich and famous, and they will stop at nothing until their fiendish plan is carried out.<br/><br/>Meanwhile, Washington</span>
  <span id="freeText9707419036562585626" style="display:none">In the middle of the night, a controversial U.S. senator is found murdered in bed in his Georgetown pied-a-terre. The police turn up only one clue: a mysterious rhyme signed "Jack and Jill" promising that this is just the beginning. Jack and Jill are out to get the rich and famous, and they will stop at nothing until their fiendish plan is carried out.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Washington, D. C., homicide detective Alex Cross is called to a murder scene only blocks from his house, far from the corridors of power where he spends his days. The victim: a beautiful little girl, savagely beaten--and desposited in front of the elementary school Cross's son, Damon, attends.<br /><br />Could there be a connection between the two murders? As Cross tries to put the pieces together, the killer- or killers - strike again. And again. No one in Washington is safe - not children, not politicians, not even the President of the United States. Only Alex Cross has the skills and the courage to crack the case-but will he discover the truth in time?<br /><br />A relentless roller coaster of heart-pounding suspense and jolting plot twists, Jack and Jill proves that no one can write a more compelling thriller than James Patterson--the master of the nonstop nightmare.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1804661298" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1804661298" />
    <a title="James Tivendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale"><img alt="James Tivendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605206526p2/10282461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1804661298?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Tivendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Tivendale" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale">James Tivendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007438044" href="/book/show/15923438-jack-and-jill">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=detective">detective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=books-to-review-q1-2017">books-to-review-q1-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1804661298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13297156873065285241">"Jack and Jill" is the third story in Patterson's gripping novels about police detective and psychologist, Dr. Alex Cross. <br/><br/>Here, we see Alex working on two of the most complex homicide cases of his already glittering career. Involving perhaps four or more different killers. Like the majority of the cases that Dr. Cross is assigned to, all involved seem to be complex and have peculiar, sometimes hidden motives. A number of the ensemble are working together to achieve their ultimate goals. In addi</span>
  <span id="freeText13297156873065285241" style="display:none">"Jack and Jill" is the third story in Patterson's gripping novels about police detective and psychologist, Dr. Alex Cross. <br /><br />Here, we see Alex working on two of the most complex homicide cases of his already glittering career. Involving perhaps four or more different killers. Like the majority of the cases that Dr. Cross is assigned to, all involved seem to be complex and have peculiar, sometimes hidden motives. A number of the ensemble are working together to achieve their ultimate goals. In addition, some of them seem to be competing for notoriety within the eyes of the nation's journalists and the general public. <br /><br />Within the crime riddled Washington D.C Alex, as always, is presented as being a loving father and good friend, just as much as he is highlighted as the most talented detective for getting into the minds of the craziest and most dangerous people on the planet. In the majority of the Alex Cross stories I have read so far, there has often been a fair amount of distress to, and violence to young children. One such case is a beautiful young girl having half of her face caved in just outside her school with a razor-wired baseball bat. These murders really hit the whole neighbourhood hard and it is a bit "too close to home" for Alex, literally as that is the school his young son Damon attends. The other targets in "Jack and Jill" are A-List celebrities and it is presented that some of the killers may perhaps have a vendetta against this way of life in America. <br /><br />If a book could be described as being a paperback equivalent to a supercar, it would be this one. It is full throttle all the way through and doesn't let up. Our metaphorical supercar doesn't go in a straight line from start to finish plot-wise either, there are thrilling twists, turns, betrayals, dust blocking where our senses should be looking etc... It contains many amazing set pieces such as hostage situations, Alex hanging out in the White House and brutal sexually influenced murders are but a few examples. In the Alex Cross stories, we get a 360 view of the action. We follow Alex in the first person, which creates affinity and adds drama as we are privy to his thoughts, internal monologue and deduction process intricately. The other characters, including Alex's, man-mountain sized best friend and partner, John Sampson and also, the killers are presented in an omnipresent third person view. Patterson occasionally flips between thoughts if multiple characters are involved in these chapters so that the reader is privy to everything going on. This builds up the tension sevenfold. <br /><br />Alex borderlines instability occasionally in some of his detective methods and still talks to a psychologist following on from the tragic murder of his wife about five years ago. In one scene he talks to one of the killers and says "I know how you feel" and his internal thoughts highlight this with a statement along the lines of ... and I really did. <br /><br />Just a short review on this one as I do not wish to give too much away. It was utterly awesome, thrilling and truly engaging. These stories are like reading a Die Hard film. "Jack and Jill" was excellent but, I think "Along Came A Spider" was very slightly better, perhaps because it was the first entry and introduction to the rotten Washington D.C where Alex has a lot more work to do in the future. <br /><br />James <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youandibooks.wordpress.com">www.youandibooks.wordpress.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13297156873065285241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2542768416" />
    <a title="Juli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38617426-juli"><img alt="Juli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453642808p2/38617426.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2542768416?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juli" href="/user/show/38617426-juli">Juli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781478976851" href="/book/show/33785689-jack-jill">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38617426-juli?shelf=read-audiobooks-2018">read-audiobooks-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38617426-juli?shelf=the-great-american-read-done">the-great-american-read-done</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2542768416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13835746396576685745">A murderous duo calling themselves Jack and Jill are killing important people in Washington, D.C. Detective Alex Cross is put on the case when they threaten the President. But he would rather stay on a more personal case....children are being killed at the school Cross' young son attends. Deaths continue as Cross investigates both cases. Is anyone in Washington safe?<br/><br/>This book is definitely filled with action and twisted suspense. Originally published in 1996, the book is a bit dated in places. B</span>
  <span id="freeText13835746396576685745" style="display:none">A murderous duo calling themselves Jack and Jill are killing important people in Washington, D.C. Detective Alex Cross is put on the case when they threaten the President. But he would rather stay on a more personal case....children are being killed at the school Cross' young son attends. Deaths continue as Cross investigates both cases. Is anyone in Washington safe?<br /><br />This book is definitely filled with action and twisted suspense. Originally published in 1996, the book is a bit dated in places. But, the story is still very much enjoyable. I found the plot in this 3rd book of the Alex Cross series to be just as action-packed and exciting as the first two books. <br /><br />I'm enjoying this series. I started reading just this year because the series is listed as part of The Great American Read. I'm not sure why I had never read a book by James Patterson before this year. I guess it was a case of so many books...only so much time. I'm glad I finally gave the Alex Cross series a try....it's really quite good. It will take me awhile to catch up, as the series has 25 books and Jack &amp; Jill is only #3. Book 26, Target, is scheduled to come out in November 2018. I have lots of reading/listening to do! <br /><br />I listened to the audio version of this book. Narrated by Ron Butler and Maxwell Hamilton, the audio is just over 12 hours long. Both narrators read at a nice pace. I liked the fact that the narrators change when the point of view changes. Even with my hearing loss, I was still able to hear and understand the entire book.<br /><br />I have book 4, Cat and Mouse, on hold at the library. I'm definitely continuing with this series. I like Alex Cross as a main character. He is gritty, intelligent and hard-hitting. I like all the side characters, especially Nana Mama and Sampson. I do see a tendency in this series towards killing or victimizing any woman that Alex looks at as a possible love interest. It's happened in every book so far....and seems repetitive and unrealistic. But, this is only book 3..... If I get further in this series and this is still a major repeating plot point, it might make me stop reading. I'm suspending judgement until I get further into the series. <br /><br />I can see why this series is part of the list of 100 books for The Great American Read. This bestselling series has wowed readers for 25 years now. The Great American Read honors 100 books that got the American public reading and talking about books. From classics to contemporary fiction, the list is varied. Check out the list here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.pbs.org/the-great-american-read/books/#/">https://www.pbs.org/the-great-america...</a> In my quest to read all 100 books/series, I am currently at 16. (I'm counting series listed as one, even if I read multiple books). Lots more reading to go! I love this concept -- I hope they do something similar again! <br /><br />Here is a link to the main website for The Great American Read: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.pbs.org/the-great-american-read/home/">https://www.pbs.org/the-great-america...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13835746396576685745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780446604802" href="/book/show/239729.Jack_Jill">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=mystery-or-crime-novel">mystery-or-crime-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=3-stars-aint-the-devil">3-stars-aint-the-devil</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3333300614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10432367005663926623"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br/><br/>When I was in the 10th grade, I went through a big James Patterson phase. My parents were buying used copies of this books for me as stocking stuffers for Christmas, and I blew through a bunch of his books. My grandmother also loved his books dearly, so when I miss her, I pick up one of his novels.<br/><br/>Say what you will about James Patterson, whether he actually wrote his books or not (I actually believe he wrote his earlier novels like this one) he’s accomplished a great thing with the Al</span>
  <span id="freeText10432367005663926623" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br /><br />When I was in the 10th grade, I went through a big James Patterson phase. My parents were buying used copies of this books for me as stocking stuffers for Christmas, and I blew through a bunch of his books. My grandmother also loved his books dearly, so when I miss her, I pick up one of his novels.<br /><br />Say what you will about James Patterson, whether he actually wrote his books or not (I actually believe he wrote his earlier novels like this one) he’s accomplished a great thing with the Alex Cross series. He has sold hundreds of millions of books, and that’s not something just anyone can brag about.<br /><br />This is the third Alex Cross novel and Alex finds himself torn between two cases: a small black girl is murdered in his neighborhood, and high profile politicians are being murdered in DC. Alex works on both at the same time, one in secret, hoping to bring justice to all the victims.<br /><br />Definitely an entertaining read. It’s been so long since I read it, I remembered almost nothing so it was like reading a new book. I do feel this style of mystery writing is outdated (mid 1990’s) and I had a hard time staying focused while reading. It didn’t really grip me like it had when I was a teen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10432367005663926623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_810997166" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/810997166" />
    <a title="Brenda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2337007-brenda"><img alt="Brenda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577750190p2/2337007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/810997166?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenda" href="/user/show/2337007-brenda">Brenda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5414726-jack-jill">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer810997166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16540160999887335943">When Detective Alex Cross was woken by his friend and partner Detective John Sampson, their destination was to Alex’s son Damon’s nearby school. The murder of the little six year old girl was sickening and hit Alex particularly hard. Their relentless search needed to be thorough; the killer needed to be found.<br/><br/>Meanwhile, a US senator was murdered in a particularly gruesome manner – Jack and Jill were on the hunt and had threatened that this was just the beginning – they promised they would strike</span>
  <span id="freeText16540160999887335943" style="display:none">When Detective Alex Cross was woken by his friend and partner Detective John Sampson, their destination was to Alex’s son Damon’s nearby school. The murder of the little six year old girl was sickening and hit Alex particularly hard. Their relentless search needed to be thorough; the killer needed to be found.<br /><br />Meanwhile, a US senator was murdered in a particularly gruesome manner – Jack and Jill were on the hunt and had threatened that this was just the beginning – they promised they would strike again…<br /><br />More bodies, more murders – Alex and Sampson were in it up to their necks. They were determined to catch the killer or killers – but were they connected? <br /><br /><i>Jack &amp; Jill</i> is the third in the Alex Cross series by James Patterson and is filled with the usual fast paced action; multiple murders and a home scene which I thoroughly enjoy. Nana Mama and the children bring a sense of normality to Alex’s life (and the series) and I always enjoy these books. Not sure why I hadn’t read this one a long time ago, but I have now! Recommended.<br /></span>

          </span>

Both stories unfold in completely unexpected ways. The Conspiracy Theorist potential of the President's predicament is realistic, humbling and frightening; while the child killer case rips the readers' heart in two. </span>

Both stories unfold in completely unexpected ways. The Conspiracy Theorist potential of the President's predicament is realistic, humbling and frightening; while the child killer case rips the readers' heart in two. The third Alex Cross novel is fabulously written and may very well keep you up late.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15558191835916384828">I thought this book was good, but not as good as the first two. It didn't draw me in like the other ones did. The ending though was intense and the only part of the book I really got into. It announced what the fourth book was going to be about by having Gary Soneji from "Along Came a Spider" reappear in the story again. I recommend this book to anyone who liked the first two of the Alex Cross series because this book leads into the story line of the fourth book which is very good.</span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14631675" />
    <a title="Bill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/810550-bill"><img alt="Bill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462234651p2/810550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14631675?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill" href="/user/show/810550-bill">Bill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/810550-bill?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14631675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17819449610219923748">While reading this one I couldn't help thinking, was Kiss the Girls really that good?<br/><br/>Patterson does have a terse writing style, but it didn't seem this bad before. It's bad here. All through reading it I was feeling like Patterson just hacked this one out of the word processor in one draft without a second glance. For a guy who writes so sparsely, he sure is repetitive throughout the story:<br/><br/>'Was Jack up ahead? Was Hawkins Jack? Was this Jack up ahead?<br/>Could this be Jack up ahead? Had we just been </span>
  <span id="freeText17819449610219923748" style="display:none">While reading this one I couldn't help thinking, was Kiss the Girls really that good?<br /><br />Patterson does have a terse writing style, but it didn't seem this bad before. It's bad here. All through reading it I was feeling like Patterson just hacked this one out of the word processor in one draft without a second glance. For a guy who writes so sparsely, he sure is repetitive throughout the story:<br /><br />'Was Jack up ahead? Was Hawkins Jack? Was this Jack up ahead?<br />Could this be Jack up ahead? Had we just been that close to catching Jack?'....<br />This within 3 pages. Who is this guy's editor, anyway?<br /><br />Another thing that bothered me was so much pop culture was thrown<br />in in an obviously contrived effort to authenticate things (Simpsons, ER, Pulp Fiction, MTV). Now you're wondering, if I hated it so much, why did I finish it? Well, I have to admit, the story itself was quite good, and I pretty much had to see it through to see how things turned out.<br />Given the right director and screenplay, this would make a terrific movie.<br />As for future Patterson efforts, I'll wait for the movies, thanks. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17819449610219923748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2222706170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer978672420739121204">Number 3 in he Alex Cross series and this time Alex has not one but two killer to hunt down.<br/>Two young children have been brutally murdered. Alex and his friend ,and fellow cop, Samson feel the need to get to the bottom of this asap. All the more so because Alex's kids attend the very same school that victims attended.<br/>To make matters worse there are two psychopathic killers (Jack & Jill) running around killing high profile citizens.<br/>Needless to say the FBI and the NYPD need Alex on the case. <br/>Alex </span>
  <span id="freeText978672420739121204" style="display:none">Number 3 in he Alex Cross series and this time Alex has not one but two killer to hunt down.<br />Two young children have been brutally murdered. Alex and his friend ,and fellow cop, Samson feel the need to get to the bottom of this asap. All the more so because Alex's kids attend the very same school that victims attended.<br />To make matters worse there are two psychopathic killers (Jack &amp; Jill) running around killing high profile citizens.<br />Needless to say the FBI and the NYPD need Alex on the case. <br />Alex finds himself trying to solve both cases at the same time, not an easy task.<br /><br />The end game, I thought, was a bit over the top. But, what the, this is make believe after all.<br />The other thing that grates on my nerves a bit was when ever Alex's kids or Nana Mama are mentioned the dialogue can be a bit cringe worthy. <br /><br />But this is just a small complainant in what proved to be a quick, enjoyable read.<br /><br />The normal <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3780.James_Patterson" title="James Patterson" rel="nofollow noopener">James Patterson</a> format. Short chapters, quick pace with the tension ranking up as the end is in site.</span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1998675-stacia?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer1606760614839244187">Reading this book is like reading a used undergraduate textbook, only it's got italics instead of highlighter. I don't think I've ever seen so many random italics to indicate words <i>the author thinks we should focus on</i>. Because apparently readers <i>aren't smart enough</i> to decide what's important and what's just ordinary narrative. And yes, it really is annoying enough that even I, a compulsive book-finisher, am considering <i>just returning this one to the library</i>.<br/><br/>Also, there's a pretty basic research </span>
  <span id="freeText1606760614839244187" style="display:none">Reading this book is like reading a used undergraduate textbook, only it's got italics instead of highlighter. I don't think I've ever seen so many random italics to indicate words <i>the author thinks we should focus on</i>. Because apparently readers <i>aren't smart enough</i> to decide what's important and what's just ordinary narrative. And yes, it really is annoying enough that even I, a compulsive book-finisher, am considering <i>just returning this one to the library</i>.<br /><br />Also, there's a pretty basic research error: the author uses "semiautomatic" and "revolver" interchangeably.<br /><br />I stopped reading about 10 pages from the end, once the "mystery" had been solved. I've read a few James Patterson books now, and I won't bother reading any more.</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/3764683-amy">Amy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201231614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5236652204949869051">This is an older Alex Cross novel. I just finished Postcard Killers (a newer novel) about a month ago, and there are a lot of similarities with the J&J killers. The biggest mystery of the book was trying to figure out why the killers did it, which is never answered completely. At the beginning J&J are playing with a game board of some kind, but that is completely forgotten after a few chapters & has nothing to do with the motive. There are too many red herrings to the point of sloppiness. When i</span>
  <span id="freeText5236652204949869051" style="display:none">This is an older Alex Cross novel. I just finished Postcard Killers (a newer novel) about a month ago, and there are a lot of similarities with the J&amp;J killers. The biggest mystery of the book was trying to figure out why the killers did it, which is never answered completely. At the beginning J&amp;J are playing with a game board of some kind, but that is completely forgotten after a few chapters &amp; has nothing to do with the motive. There are too many red herrings to the point of sloppiness. When it comes to the end, you're scratching you head b/c there were not any clues to the identity of the killers.<br />Alex Cross has another case with children being murdered in a schoolyard. Again, too many red herrings and the killer's motive never is clearly seen. The killer is only after black children and you never know if it was just opportunity or racism.<br />A point of note is that the future Mrs. Cross, Christine, is introduced.<br />The reason I bought the audio was because John Rubinstein did part of the audio. He does the John Kellerman audios and in this plays all the killer's voices. Blair Underwood is the voice of Cross and he is awful. I may be biased, but I wanted Morgan Freeman because Underwood read too fast &amp; it's hard to keep up the change in scene. Rubinstein was wonderful and did not jell will Underwood.<br />Even with Rubinstein, I do not recommend this novel. The police work is sloppy and Cross never catches or IDs the killers. They make mistakes or turn on each other. You are never told a motive or if the Real Jack is playing the board game with the Real Jill or the Fake Jill. This book is a waste. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5236652204949869051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14801518350377889767">This will contain a few minor spoilers but should not ruin the book for anyone.<br/>I have to admit I did not read the first two books but I did see the movie and I tend to get bored reading books AFTER seeing the movies so I skipped them. It was not hard to "catch up" on this one tho. <br/>While James Patterson is a good writer and a well known author I don't think this was one of his better books sadly. I think there were a lot of questions left unanswered and things just thrown in. I wanted to know mor</span>
  <span id="freeText14801518350377889767" style="display:none">This will contain a few minor spoilers but should not ruin the book for anyone.<br />I have to admit I did not read the first two books but I did see the movie and I tend to get bored reading books AFTER seeing the movies so I skipped them. It was not hard to "catch up" on this one tho. <br />While James Patterson is a good writer and a well known author I don't think this was one of his better books sadly. I think there were a lot of questions left unanswered and things just thrown in. I wanted to know more about the game "Jack and Jill" were playing and why they were playing the board game. Neither one of the motivates were ever explained and when the true killers were caught at the end it just didn't fit for me. I was like huh? It just felt as if it didn't fit.<br />Minor Spoiler here---- <br />When Christine's husband gets shot and killed I sort of felt like it was a way Alex could finally be with her without it seeming so horrible. You never meet her husband or know how she feels about his up until this point but you know how Alex feels about her every time he see's her to the point it gets annoying and obsessive.<br />I have always liked James Patterson tho and have a hard time giving his books less then three stars and maybe this one did deserve two but the writing was good and I will read at least a few more in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14801518350377889767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/208086589?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Crosse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Crosse" href="/user/show/3181880-laura-crosse">Laura Crosse</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer208086589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15308422939840380580">This may have been the best Patterson novel I've ever read including all stand-alone's and other series of his, it was that good! It was full of action from the get-go especially that there wasn't just one killer, there wasn't even just two, there was three. Two working together as Jack and Jill who are murdering well known celebrities and then also the Truth School killer who's murdering little kids. Both are shocking cases but maybe for different reasons. <br/><br/>There is an element of racism in this </span>
  <span id="freeText15308422939840380580" style="display:none">This may have been the best Patterson novel I've ever read including all stand-alone's and other series of his, it was that good! It was full of action from the get-go especially that there wasn't just one killer, there wasn't even just two, there was three. Two working together as Jack and Jill who are murdering well known celebrities and then also the Truth School killer who's murdering little kids. Both are shocking cases but maybe for different reasons. <br /><br />There is an element of racism in this book as their seems to be with all of the Cross novels. The kids being killed by the Truth School killer are black and the celebrities are both white, rich and powerful, so guess who gets the most attention from the police force in Washington? Of course Alex contests this strongly but is forced into working more on the Jack and Jill case by his superiors. He still works on the child murders as much as he can though proving how a lovely, honest character he truely is. <br /><br />The whole element with the President assassination was really gripping and I thought it was quite brave of an author to tackle something so monumentally huge. It really is the biggest crime you could probably commit in America and it will write you into the history books, something Jack and Jill are counting on. Very good book, gripping and how a thriller should be. Thrilling!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15308422939840380580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1755791207" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11353586549169908955">First 150 pages are very slow, I won't say dull but frankly they are not very interesting. Then the story picks up and it becomes a page turner. Full of racism, difference between victims is perfectly portrayed. Jack and Jill are killing rich and powerful white celebrities while Truth School Killer's victims are black kids.   <span id="freeText11353586549169908955" style="display:none">First 150 pages are very slow, I won't say dull but frankly they are not very interesting. Then the story picks up and it becomes a page turner. Full of racism, difference between victims is perfectly portrayed. Jack and Jill are killing rich and powerful white celebrities while Truth School Killer's victims are black kids. Guess who gets all attention. <br /><br />The whole element with the President assassination was really gripping and I thought it was quite brave of an author to tackle something so huge. Stirring ghosts from the real world where both Kennedy brothers have been assassinated and their death is still subject of widespread analysis.<br /><br />It really is the biggest crime you could probably commit not just in the U.S. but also around the globe, this is a act that will put you into the history books, something Jack and Jill are counting on. Very good book (not awesome), gripping and how a thriller should be. Thrilling!<br /><br />I was hoping for Alex to finally mange to discover who stands behind president assassination but I guess it is one of the many parallels drawn between fictional and real world!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8430001451289210789">One of the things that enriches the character of Alex Cross is his family. It makes him seem more real and shows a dimension of his humanity that goes beyond his work. This story is made more intense by the threat his work sometimes brings home to his family. When tracking a serial killer, it can become difficult to determine exactly who is the prey and who is the predator.<br/><br/>The two simultaneous cases that Alex works in this story serve up plenty of tension and excitement. A child killer strikes c</span>
  <span id="freeText8430001451289210789" style="display:none">One of the things that enriches the character of Alex Cross is his family. It makes him seem more real and shows a dimension of his humanity that goes beyond his work. This story is made more intense by the threat his work sometimes brings home to his family. When tracking a serial killer, it can become difficult to determine exactly who is the prey and who is the predator.<br /><br />The two simultaneous cases that Alex works in this story serve up plenty of tension and excitement. A child killer strikes close to home when a little girl is found dead near his son's school. But at the same time, a pair of psychos who go by the names Jack and Jill start a spectacular series of celebrity killings. The child killer is a personal matter as much as a professional one, but Alex is forced by his chief to put most of his energy into the Jack and Jill case.<br /><br />As is typical of this series, the character of the killers is nearly as developed as that of the "good guys," which can be quite disturbing at times. In spite of that, this book was a page-turner.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8430001451289210789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8025744236542694559">Jack & Jill (Alex Cross #3)<br/><br/>There isn't much I can say about the book or the author. I love the Alex Cross series. I was hooked with "A Long Came a Spider," and "Kiss the Girls."<br/><br/>Jack and Jill is a fast pace, riveting, suspense/thriller. Plot development received excellent support from its chapter development and suspenseful sub-</span>
  <span id="freeText8025744236542694559" style="display:none">Jack &amp; Jill (Alex Cross #3)<br /><br />There isn't much I can say about the book or the author. I love the Alex Cross series. I was hooked with "A Long Came a Spider," and "Kiss the Girls."<br /><br />Jack and Jill is a fast pace, riveting, suspense/thriller. This is a novel I would love to watch on the big screen!<br /><br />James Patterson is an Master at character development, which is such an essential element in the craft of writing. Plot development received excellent support from its chapter development and suspenseful sub-plotting. <br /><br />Jack and Jill is an assassination team that terrorize the DC area, and puts Capital Hill on high alert. they are highly skilled, highly effective, and Alex is placed right in the middle of their carnage and rampage to execute the President of the United States.<br /><br />So go find your favorite chair, a pot of coffee, or coco, and whatever else you need to be comfortable, while James takes you on this emotional roller-coaster with Alex Cross to uncover the reason why these ghost has come out to kill in this 5 star read.<br /><br />~LW~<br /><br /></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2763719-john?shelf=mystery-detective-fiction">mystery-detective-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2763719-john?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer465794755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16729610759838503041">With JACK & JILL, the Alex Cross series--which began with the quite entertaining ALONG CAME A SPIDER--simply falls of a cliff. The writing is absolutely HORRENDOUS, even by James Patterson standards. Had I not known better, I might have thought it was written by a high school kid. The character of Alex Cross doesn't fare very well here, either. Like most people, I enjoy smart detective novels that feature smart detectives doing smart detecting. Unfortunately, there's precious little of that to b</span>
  <span id="freeText16729610759838503041" style="display:none">With JACK &amp; JILL, the Alex Cross series--which began with the quite entertaining ALONG CAME A SPIDER--simply falls of a cliff. The writing is absolutely HORRENDOUS, even by James Patterson standards. Had I not known better, I might have thought it was written by a high school kid. The character of Alex Cross doesn't fare very well here, either. Like most people, I enjoy smart detective novels that feature smart detectives doing smart detecting. Unfortunately, there's precious little of that to be found in JACK &amp; Jill. Here, Alex Cross seems able to find a killer only so long as the killer is handed to him on a silver platter. In addition, Cross takes some pretty stupid risks in this novel, and it's only because Patterson needs him in future novels that he isn't killed in some incredibly anticlimactic way. JACK &amp; JILL is easily one of the most amateurishly written best-sellers I've ever read. It makes Dan Brown look like Dostoyevsky. I seriously doubt whether Patterson took the time to produce more than a single draft, and I find it even harder to imagine that the manuscript was ever looked at by a professional editor. Definitely a low point in '90's pop literature. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16729610759838503041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198950747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9541425044048798658">Alex Cross is back in this, the third installment from top-selling American author, James Patterson. <br/>The action starts with the murder of a US Senator. Closer to home, a young girl is also found dead. The body-count soon starts to mount and Homicide Detective Alex Cross becomes the go-to man. Cross is torn between the two seemingly unrelated serial murder cases. The young children being murdered attend Cross's own sons school and therefore have personal significance for Cross. But the political </span>
  <span id="freeText9541425044048798658" style="display:none">Alex Cross is back in this, the third installment from top-selling American author, James Patterson. <br />The action starts with the murder of a US Senator. Closer to home, a young girl is also found dead. The body-count soon starts to mount and Homicide Detective Alex Cross becomes the go-to man. Cross is torn between the two seemingly unrelated serial murder cases. The young children being murdered attend Cross's own sons school and therefore have personal significance for Cross. But the political crimes are high profile and a nation wants the killer(s) caught. Perhaps the deaths are related? <br />Like all Patterson books, the writing style is fast-paced and punchy. The chapters are short, with each small chapter hooking the reader into the next one. The pages fly by rapidly, and this trademark style makes for a quick, but absorbing read. Patterson officianados will enjoy this novel as much as any other. And whilst the Patterson production line is not yet in full swing, the framework and formula that will launch many more books in the future definitely is. You know what you are getting with a James Patterson thriller, and this is no exception. An entertaining, yet easy-to-read thriller.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9541425044048798658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney" href="/user/show/10767506-courtney">Courtney</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer363846941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14768737682078205105">Jack & Jill gives a creepy insight into the inter-workings of our government. Although, it is a fiction novel, Im sure the plans that took place in this novel have been attempted before. <br/><br/><br/>Jack & Jill are two high profile killers in Washington D.C. They kill people that are held high in the public eye and are working their way towards their ultimate goal -- Killing the real Jack & Jill -- Mr. and Mrs. President of the United States. <br/><br/><br/>Can Alex Cross catch them before it is too late?<br/><br/>At the same time,</span>
  <span id="freeText14768737682078205105" style="display:none">Jack &amp; Jill gives a creepy insight into the inter-workings of our government. Although, it is a fiction novel, Im sure the plans that took place in this novel have been attempted before. <br /><br /><br />Jack &amp; Jill are two high profile killers in Washington D.C. They kill people that are held high in the public eye and are working their way towards their ultimate goal -- Killing the real Jack &amp; Jill -- Mr. and Mrs. President of the United States. <br /><br /><br />Can Alex Cross catch them before it is too late?<br /><br />At the same time, there are mysterious children murders happening in Cross's neighborhood. With his heart in trying to solve the case, he gets pulled off and put on the Jack and Jill case.<br />He goes undercover with his partner Sampson and a few guys from their department to try to solve the cases themselves. The cases aren't getting much attention because of the high profile murders. <br /><br />This novel is fast paced and keeps you guessing until Patterson is ready to reveal the whole story to you. The Jack and Jill killings were intimate but lacking emotions. The child murders left me quite sad and cringing. <br /><br />Patterson nails another great book. <br /><br />4/5 stars. There were a few boring parts, but over all exciting!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14768737682078205105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0cp+NWf24Y2DyOU9tijIh+Rvhrk09mo9+0IWL2t0VMKEQraQXjUQeykADbbexSpretCJtWz5JiWOqUjC5XjNuw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Yd9S8MGdHj01rUlf8Fllc6YUJ3jWIyBH70dhmZ+cK6I0V5pV+F7vy59lodSYtIefOKsodI4sbF+arD90EZCy2w==')})
  }

The future of the paper looked grim until a young mother was brutally raped and murdered by a member of the notorious Padgitt family. Willie Traynor reported all the gruesome details, and his newspaper began to prosper.The murderer, Danny Padgitt, was tried before a packed courthouse in Clanton, Mississippi. The trial came to a startling and dramatic end when the defendant threatened revenge against the jurors if they convicted him. Nevertheless, they found him guilty, and he was sentenced to life in prison. But in Mississippi in 1970, life didn\'t necessarily mean life, and nine years later Danny Padgitt managed to get himself paroled. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7165390106530972893"><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official US Site</a><br/><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official UK Site</a><br/><a href='http://jimmypatterson.org' rel='nofollow noopener'>JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br/><a href='http://readkiddoread.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>ReadKiddoRead</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books wo</span>
  <span id="freeText7165390106530972893" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Official US Site</a><br /><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Official UK Site</a><br /><a href="http://jimmypatterson.org" rel="nofollow noopener">JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br /><a href="http://readkiddoread.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadKiddoRead</a><br /><br /><br /><br />James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books worldwide and currently holds the Guinness World Record for the most #1 New York Times bestsellers. In addition to writing the thriller novels for which he is best known, among them The President Is Missing with President Bill Clinton, Patterson also writes fiction for young readers of all ages, including the Max Einstein series, produced in partnership with the Albert Einstein Estate. He is also the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on the New York Times adult and children’s bestseller lists.<br /> <br />The son of an insurance salesman and a schoolteacher, Patterson grew up in Newburgh, New York, and began casually writing at the age of nineteen. In 1969, he graduated from Manhattan College. He was given a full-ride scholarship to Vanderbilt University’s graduate program in English. He left Vanderbilt before getting his PhD due to complications involving the Vietnam War. <br /> <br />Instead, he moved to New York to become a junior copywriter for the advertising agency J. Walter Thompson, eventually becoming CEO of its North American company.<br /> <br />In 1976, while still working for J. Walter Thompson, Patterson published his first novel, The Thomas Berryman Number, with Little, Brown and Company. After being turned down by thirty-one publishers, it won the Edgar Award for Best First Novel. Patterson’s 1993 novel, Along Came a Spider, his first book to feature Alex Cross, was also his first New York Times bestseller in fiction.<br /> <br />In 2001, Morgan Freeman starred as Alex Cross in a film adaptation of Along Came a Spider, and Tyler Perry also played the character in the 2012 film Alex Cross. A film adaptation of Patterson’s middle-grade novel Middle School: The Worst Years of My Life was released in theaters in October 2016.<br /> <br />James Patterson has donated more than one million books to students, focusing on some of the most under-resourced schools and youth programs in the country. To date, he has donated $7.25 million to school and classroom libraries throughout the United States, and $2.1 million to independent bookstores and employees.<br /> <br />Patterson has recently donated over $35 million to his and his wife’s alma maters—the University of Wisconsin, Vanderbilt University, and Manhattan College—and he has established over four hundred Teacher and Writer Education Scholarships at twenty-one colleges and universities throughout the country. Patterson has also donated more than one million books to U.S. soldiers at home and overseas.<br /> <br />In May 2015, Patterson launched a children’s book imprint at Little, Brown—JIMMY Patterson—that is unwaveringly focused on one goal: turning kids into lifelong readers. This imprint also provides resources, strategies, and programs to serve teachers, parents, librarians, and booksellers. Patterson invests proceeds from the sales of JIMMY Patterson Books in pro-reading initiatives.<br /> <br />Patterson also founded ReadKiddoRead.com, a website designed to help parents, teachers, and librarians ignite a new generation’s excitement for reading. Awarded the National Book Foundation’s Innovations in Reading Prize and the American Library Association’s Great Websites for Kids, the site features thoughtful book reviews from a variety of genres and age ranges, a large and lively Facebook community, and contributions from other authors.<br /> <br />Patterson’s awards for adult and children’s literature include the Edgar Award, the International </span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_13151').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_13151').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_13151').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script>
